	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Bernard Montgomery</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bernard_Montgomery,_1st_Viscount_Montgomery_of_Alamein&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Bernard Montgomery, 1st Viscount Montgomery of Alamein">Bernard Montgomery, 1st Viscount Montgomery of Alamein</a>)</span></div>

<p><a href="/wiki/Field_marshal_(United_Kingdom)" title="Field marshal (United Kingdom)">Field Marshal</a> <b>Bernard Law Montgomery, 1st Viscount Montgomery of Alamein</b>, <span class="noexcerpt" style="font-size:100;"><a href="/wiki/Knight_of_the_Order_of_the_Garter" class="mw-redirect" title="Knight of the Order of the Garter">KG</a><span style="font-size:14px;">&#44;</span>&#32;<a href="/wiki/Knight_Grand_Cross_of_the_Order_of_the_Bath" class="mw-redirect" title="Knight Grand Cross of the Order of the Bath">GCB</a><span style="font-size:14px;">&#44;</span>&#32;<a href="/wiki/Distinguished_Service_Order" title="Distinguished Service Order">DSO</a><span style="font-size:14px;">&#44;</span>&#32;<a href="/wiki/Privy_Council_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Privy Council of the United Kingdom">PC</a><span style="font-size:14px;">&#44;</span>&#32;<a href="/wiki/Deputy_Lieutenant" class="mw-redirect" title="Deputy Lieutenant">DL</a></span> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/ɡ/: &#39;g&#39; in &#39;guy&#39;">ɡ</span><span title="/ʌ/: &#39;u&#39; in &#39;cut&#39;">ʌ</span><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span><span title="/ər/: &#39;er&#39; in &#39;letter&#39;">ər</span><span title="/i/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;happy&#39;">i</span></span>&#8201;...&#8201;<wbr /><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/æ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">æ</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span><span title="/eɪ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;face&#39;">eɪ</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span></span>/</a></span></span>; 17 November 1887&#160;– 24 March 1976), nicknamed "<b>Monty</b>" and "<b>The Spartan General</b>",<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> was a senior <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British Army</a> <a href="/wiki/Officer_(armed_forces)" title="Officer (armed forces)">officer</a> who fought in both the <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">First World War</a> and the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">Second World War</a>.
</p><p>He first saw action in the First World War as a junior officer of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Warwickshire_Regiment" title="Royal Warwickshire Regiment">Royal Warwickshire Regiment</a>. At <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A9teren" title="Méteren">Méteren</a>, near the Belgian border at <a href="/wiki/Bailleul,_Nord" title="Bailleul, Nord">Bailleul</a>, he was shot through the right lung by a sniper, during the <a href="/wiki/First_Battle_of_Ypres" title="First Battle of Ypres">First Battle of Ypres</a>. He returned to the <a href="/wiki/Western_Front_(World_War_I)" title="Western Front (World War I)">Western Front</a> as a general staff officer and took part in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Arras_(1917)" title="Battle of Arras (1917)">Battle of Arras</a> in April/May 1917. He also took part in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Passchendaele" title="Battle of Passchendaele">Battle of Passchendaele</a> in late 1917 before finishing the war as <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_staff" title="Chief of staff">chief of staff</a> of the <a href="/wiki/47th_(1/2nd_London)_Division" title="47th (1/2nd London) Division">47th (2nd London) Division</a>.
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Interwar_period" title="Interwar period">inter-war years</a> he commanded the 17th (Service) Battalion, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Fusiliers" title="Royal Fusiliers">Royal Fusiliers</a> and, later, the 1st Battalion, Royal Warwickshire Regiment before becoming commander of <a href="/wiki/9th_Infantry_Brigade_(United_Kingdom)" title="9th Infantry Brigade (United Kingdom)">9th Infantry Brigade</a> and then <a href="/wiki/General_officer_commanding" title="General officer commanding">General Officer Commanding</a> (GOC) <a href="/wiki/8th_Infantry_Division_(United_Kingdom)" title="8th Infantry Division (United Kingdom)">8th Infantry Division</a>.
</p><p>During the Second World War he commanded the <a href="/wiki/Eighth_Army_(United_Kingdom)" title="Eighth Army (United Kingdom)">British Eighth Army</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Western_Desert_Campaign" class="mw-redirect" title="Western Desert Campaign">Western Desert</a> from August 1942 until the final <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied</a> <a href="/wiki/Tunisia_Campaign" class="mw-redirect" title="Tunisia Campaign">victory in Tunisia</a> in May 1943. This period included the <a href="/wiki/Second_Battle_of_El_Alamein" title="Second Battle of El Alamein">Second Battle of El Alamein</a>. He subsequently commanded the British Eighth Army during the <a href="/wiki/Allied_invasion_of_Sicily" title="Allied invasion of Sicily">Allied invasion of Sicily</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Allied_invasion_of_Italy" title="Allied invasion of Italy">Allied invasion of Italy</a>. He was in command of all Allied ground forces during <a href="/wiki/Operation_Overlord" title="Operation Overlord">Operation <i>Overlord</i></a> from the initial landings until the end of the <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Normandy" title="Invasion of Normandy">Battle of Normandy</a>. He then continued in command of the <a href="/wiki/21st_Army_Group" title="21st Army Group">21st Army Group</a> for the rest of the <a href="/wiki/North_West_Europe_Campaign" class="mw-redirect" title="North West Europe Campaign">campaign in North West Europe</a>. His 21st Army Group failed in their airborne attempt to bridge the Rhine under <a href="/wiki/Operation_Market_Garden" title="Operation Market Garden">Operation Market Garden</a>, after being defeated in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Arnhem" title="Battle of Arnhem">Battle of Arnhem</a>. When German armoured forces broke through the American lines in Belgium months later in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Bulge" title="Battle of the Bulge">Battle of the Bulge</a>, Montgomery was given command of the north shoulder of the Bulge. This included temporary command of the <a href="/wiki/First_United_States_Army" title="First United States Army">US First Army</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ninth_United_States_Army" title="Ninth United States Army">US Ninth Army</a>, which held up the German advance in the north of the Bulge while the US Third Army under Patton relieved Bastogne from the south. Montgomery's 21st Army Group, bolstered by the US Ninth Army and the <a href="/wiki/First_Allied_Airborne_Army" title="First Allied Airborne Army">First Allied Airborne Army</a>, crossed the Rhine in <a href="/wiki/Operation_Plunder" title="Operation Plunder">Operation Plunder</a> in March 1945, two weeks after the US First Army had crossed the Rhine in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Remagen" title="Battle of Remagen">Battle of Remagen</a>. On 4 May 1945 Montgomery accepted the surrender of the German forces in North-western Europe at <a href="/wiki/German_surrender_at_L%C3%BCneburg_Heath" title="German surrender at Lüneburg Heath">Lüneburg Heath</a>, east of <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a>, after the surrender of Berlin to the USSR on 2 May but before the general surrender to SHAEF on 7 May.
</p><p>After the war he became Commander-in-Chief of the <a href="/wiki/British_Army_of_the_Rhine" title="British Army of the Rhine">British Army of the Rhine</a> (BAOR) in Germany and then <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_the_General_Staff_(United_Kingdom)" title="Chief of the General Staff (United Kingdom)">Chief of the Imperial General Staff</a> (1946–1948). From 1948 to 1951 he served as Chairman of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Union_(alliance)#Commanders-in-Chief_Committee" title="Western Union (alliance)">Commanders-in-Chief Committee</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Union_(alliance)" title="Western Union (alliance)">Western Union</a>. He then served as <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>'s Deputy <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Allied_Commander_Europe" title="Supreme Allied Commander Europe">Supreme Allied Commander Europe</a> until his retirement in 1958.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bernard_Montgomery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Montgomery was born in <a href="/wiki/Kennington" title="Kennington">Kennington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Surrey" title="Surrey">Surrey</a>, in 1887, the fourth child of nine, to an <a href="/wiki/Ulster-Scots_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Ulster-Scots people">Ulster-Scots</a> <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Ireland" title="Church of Ireland">Church of Ireland</a> <a href="/wiki/Minister_(Christianity)" title="Minister (Christianity)">minister</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Reverend" title="The Reverend">The Reverend</a> <a href="/wiki/Henry_Montgomery_(bishop)" title="Henry Montgomery (bishop)">Henry Montgomery</a>, and his wife, Maud (<i>née</i> Farrar).<sup id="cite_ref-hamilton3_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hamilton3-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The Montgomerys, an '<a href="/wiki/Protestant_Ascendancy" title="Protestant Ascendancy">Ascendancy</a>' <a href="/wiki/Gentry" title="Gentry">gentry</a> family, were the <a href="/wiki/County_Donegal" title="County Donegal">County Donegal</a> branch of the <a href="/wiki/Clan_Montgomery" title="Clan Montgomery">Clan Montgomery</a>. Henry Montgomery, at that time <a href="/wiki/Vicar" title="Vicar">Vicar</a> of <a href="/wiki/St_Mark%27s_Church,_Kennington" title="St Mark&#39;s Church, Kennington">St Mark's Church</a>, Kennington, was the second son of <a href="/wiki/Sir_Robert_Montgomery" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Robert Montgomery">Sir Robert Montgomery</a>, a native of <a href="/wiki/Inishowen" title="Inishowen">Inishowen</a> in <a href="/wiki/County_Donegal" title="County Donegal">County Donegal</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ulster" title="Ulster">Ulster</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> the noted colonial administrator in <a href="/wiki/British_India" class="mw-redirect" title="British India">British India</a>, who died a month after his grandson's birth.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> He was probably a descendant of <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Montgomery_(1686%E2%80%931729)" title="Alexander Montgomery (1686–1729)">Colonel Alexander Montgomery</a> (1686–1729). Bernard's mother, Maud, was the daughter of <a href="/wiki/The_Very_Reverend" title="The Very Reverend">The V. Rev.</a> <a href="/wiki/Frederic_William_Farrar" class="mw-redirect" title="Frederic William Farrar">Frederic William Canon Farrar</a>, the famous preacher, and was eighteen years younger than her husband.<sup id="cite_ref-hamilton3_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hamilton3-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> After the death of Sir Robert Montgomery, Henry inherited the Montgomery ancestral estate of New Park in <a href="/wiki/Moville,_County_Donegal" class="mw-redirect" title="Moville, County Donegal">Moville</a> in <a href="/wiki/Inishowen" title="Inishowen">Inishowen</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ulster" title="Ulster">Ulster</a>. There was still £13,000 to pay on a <a href="/wiki/Mortgage_loan" title="Mortgage loan">mortgage</a>, a large debt in the 1880s, and Henry was at the time still only an <a href="/wiki/Anglican" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglican">Anglican</a> <a href="/wiki/Vicar" title="Vicar">vicar</a>. Despite selling off all the farms that were at Ballynally, "there was barely enough to keep up New Park and pay for the blasted summer holiday" (i.e., at New Park).<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>It was a financial relief of some magnitude when, in 1889, Henry was made <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Tasmania" class="mw-redirect" title="Bishop of Tasmania">Bishop of Tasmania</a>, then still a <a href="/wiki/British_colony" class="mw-redirect" title="British colony">British colony</a> and Bernard spent his formative years there. <a href="/wiki/Bishop" title="Bishop">Bishop</a> Montgomery considered it his duty to spend as much time as possible in the rural areas of <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Tasmania" title="Colony of Tasmania">Tasmania</a> and was away for up to six months at a time. While he was away, his wife, still in her mid-twenties, gave her children "constant" beatings,<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> then ignored them most of the time as she performed the public duties of the bishop's wife. Of Bernard's siblings, Sibyl died prematurely in Tasmania, and Harold, Donald and Una all emigrated.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Maud Montgomery took little active interest in the education of her young children other than to have them taught by tutors brought from Britain. The loveless environment made Bernard something of a bully, as he himself recalled, "I was a dreadful little boy. I don't suppose anybody would put up with my sort of behaviour these days."<sup id="cite_ref-chalfont_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chalfont-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Later in life Montgomery refused to allow his son <a href="/wiki/David_Montgomery,_2nd_Viscount_Montgomery_of_Alamein" title="David Montgomery, 2nd Viscount Montgomery of Alamein">David</a> to have anything to do with his grandmother, and refused to attend her funeral in 1949.<sup id="cite_ref-biermansmith_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biermansmith-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The family returned to England once for a <a href="/wiki/Lambeth_Conference" title="Lambeth Conference">Lambeth Conference</a> in 1897, and Bernard and his brother Harold were educated for a term at <a href="/wiki/The_King%27s_School,_Canterbury" title="The King&#39;s School, Canterbury">The King's School, Canterbury</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> In 1901, Bishop Montgomery became secretary of the <a href="/wiki/Society_for_the_Propagation_of_the_Gospel" class="mw-redirect" title="Society for the Propagation of the Gospel">Society for the Propagation of the Gospel</a>, and the family returned to London. Montgomery attended <a href="/wiki/St_Paul%27s_School_(London)" class="mw-redirect" title="St Paul&#39;s School (London)">St Paul's School</a> and then the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Military_College,_Sandhurst" title="Royal Military College, Sandhurst">Royal Military College, Sandhurst</a>, from which he was almost expelled for rowdiness and violence.<sup id="cite_ref-heath213_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heath213-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> On graduation in September 1908 he was commissioned into the 1st Battalion the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Warwickshire_Regiment" title="Royal Warwickshire Regiment">Royal Warwickshire Regiment</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Second_lieutenant" title="Second lieutenant">second lieutenant</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> and first saw overseas service later that year in <a href="/wiki/British_India" class="mw-redirect" title="British India">India</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-heath213_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heath213-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> He was promoted to <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_(British_Army_and_Royal_Marines)" title="Lieutenant (British Army and Royal Marines)">lieutenant</a> in 1910,<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> and in 1912 became adjutant of the 1st Battalion of his regiment at <a href="/wiki/Shorncliffe_Army_Camp" title="Shorncliffe Army Camp">Shorncliffe Army Camp</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-heath213_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heath213-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Montgomery_First_World_War.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Montgomery_First_World_War.jpg/170px-Montgomery_First_World_War.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="228" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Montgomery_First_World_War.jpg/255px-Montgomery_First_World_War.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Montgomery_First_World_War.jpg/340px-Montgomery_First_World_War.jpg 2x" data-file-width="423" data-file-height="567" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Montgomery_First_World_War.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bernard L. Montgomery, <a href="/wiki/Distinguished_Service_Order" title="Distinguished Service Order">DSO</a> (pictured on the right as a <a href="/wiki/Captain_(British_Army_and_Royal_Marines)" title="Captain (British Army and Royal Marines)">captain</a>), with a fellow officer of <a href="/wiki/104th_Brigade_(United_Kingdom)" title="104th Brigade (United Kingdom)">104th Brigade</a>, <a href="/wiki/35th_Division_(United_Kingdom)" title="35th Division (United Kingdom)">35th Division</a>. Montgomery served with the brigade from January 1915 until early 1917.</div></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="First_World_War">First World War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bernard_Montgomery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: First World War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">Great War</a> began in August 1914 and Montgomery moved to France with his battalion that month, which was at the time part of the <a href="/wiki/10th_Infantry_Brigade_(United_Kingdom)" title="10th Infantry Brigade (United Kingdom)">10th Brigade</a> of the <a href="/wiki/4th_Infantry_Division_(United_Kingdom)" title="4th Infantry Division (United Kingdom)">4th Division</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-heath213_21-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heath213-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> He saw action at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Le_Cateau" title="Battle of Le Cateau">Battle of Le Cateau</a> that month and during the retreat from <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Mons" title="Battle of Mons">Mons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-heath213_21-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heath213-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A9teren" title="Méteren">Méteren</a>, near the Belgian border at <a href="/wiki/Bailleul,_Nord" title="Bailleul, Nord">Bailleul</a> on 13 October 1914, during an Allied counter-offensive, he was shot through the right <a href="/wiki/Human_lung" class="mw-redirect" title="Human lung">lung</a> by a sniper.<sup id="cite_ref-heath213_21-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heath213-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Montgomery was hit once more, in the knee.<sup id="cite_ref-biermansmith_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biermansmith-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> He was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Distinguished_Service_Order" title="Distinguished Service Order">Distinguished Service Order</a> for gallant leadership: the citation for this award, published in the <i><a href="/wiki/London_Gazette" class="mw-redirect" title="London Gazette">London Gazette</a></i> in December 1914 reads:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886047036">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Conspicuous gallant leading on 13th October, when he turned the enemy out of their trenches with the bayonet. He was severely wounded.<sup id="cite_ref-DSO_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DSO-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<p>After recovering in early 1915, he was appointed <a href="/wiki/Brigade_major" title="Brigade major">brigade major</a><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> first of <a href="/wiki/112th_Brigade_(United_Kingdom)" title="112th Brigade (United Kingdom)">112th Brigade</a> and then with <a href="/wiki/104th_Brigade_(United_Kingdom)" title="104th Brigade (United Kingdom)">104th Brigade</a> under training in <a href="/wiki/Lancashire" title="Lancashire">Lancashire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-heath214_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heath214-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> He returned to the <a href="/wiki/Western_Front_(World_War_I)" title="Western Front (World War I)">Western Front</a> in early 1916 as a general staff officer in the <a href="/wiki/33rd_Division_(United_Kingdom)" title="33rd Division (United Kingdom)">33rd Division</a> and took part in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Arras_(1917)" title="Battle of Arras (1917)">Battle of Arras</a> in April/May 1917.<sup id="cite_ref-heath214_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heath214-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> He became a general staff officer with <a href="/wiki/IX_Corps_(United_Kingdom)" title="IX Corps (United Kingdom)">IX Corps</a>, part of <a href="/wiki/General_(United_Kingdom)" title="General (United Kingdom)">General</a> <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Plumer,_1st_Viscount_Plumer" title="Herbert Plumer, 1st Viscount Plumer">Sir Herbert Plumer</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Second_Army_(United_Kingdom)" title="Second Army (United Kingdom)">Second Army</a>, in July 1917.<sup id="cite_ref-heath214_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heath214-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Hundred_Days_Offensive,_August-november_1918_Q11428.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/The_Hundred_Days_Offensive%2C_August-november_1918_Q11428.jpg/220px-The_Hundred_Days_Offensive%2C_August-november_1918_Q11428.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/The_Hundred_Days_Offensive%2C_August-november_1918_Q11428.jpg/330px-The_Hundred_Days_Offensive%2C_August-november_1918_Q11428.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/The_Hundred_Days_Offensive%2C_August-november_1918_Q11428.jpg/440px-The_Hundred_Days_Offensive%2C_August-november_1918_Q11428.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="591" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Hundred_Days_Offensive,_August-november_1918_Q11428.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Minister of Munitions, Winston Churchill, watching the march past of the 47th (2nd London) Division in the Grande Place, Lille. In front of him is the Chief of Staff of the 47th Division, Lieutenant-Colonel Bernard Montgomery.</div></div></div>
<p>Montgomery served at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Passchendaele" title="Battle of Passchendaele">Battle of Passchendaele</a> in late 1917 before finishing the war as GSO1 (effectively <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_staff" title="Chief of staff">Chief of Staff</a>) of the <a href="/wiki/47th_(1/2nd_London)_Division" title="47th (1/2nd London) Division">47th (2nd London) Division</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-heath214_26-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heath214-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> with the temporary rank of <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_colonel_(United_Kingdom)" title="Lieutenant colonel (United Kingdom)">lieutenant colonel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> A photograph from October 1918, reproduced in many biographies, shows the then unknown Lieutenant Colonel Montgomery standing in front of <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> (then the <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_Munitions" title="Minister of Munitions">Minister of Munitions</a>) at the parade following the liberation of <a href="/wiki/Lille" title="Lille">Lille</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Between_the_world_wars">Between the world wars</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bernard_Montgomery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Between the world wars">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1920s">1920s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bernard_Montgomery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1920s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After the First World War Montgomery commanded the 17th (Service) Battalion of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Fusiliers" title="Royal Fusiliers">Royal Fusiliers</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> a battalion in the <a href="/wiki/British_Army_of_the_Rhine" title="British Army of the Rhine">British Army of the Rhine</a>, before reverting to his substantive rank of <a href="/wiki/Captain_(British_Army_and_Royal_Marines)" title="Captain (British Army and Royal Marines)">captain</a> (<a href="/wiki/Brevet_(military)" title="Brevet (military)">brevet</a> <a href="/wiki/Major_(United_Kingdom)" title="Major (United Kingdom)">major</a>) in November 1919.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> He had not at first been selected for the <a href="/wiki/Staff_College,_Camberley" title="Staff College, Camberley">Staff College in Camberley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Surrey" title="Surrey">Surrey</a> (his only hope of ever achieving high command). But at a tennis party in <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a>, he was able to persuade the <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" title="Commander-in-chief">Commander-in-Chief</a> (C-in-C) of the <a href="/wiki/British_Army_of_the_Rhine" title="British Army of the Rhine">British Army of Occupation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Field_marshal_(United_Kingdom)" title="Field marshal (United Kingdom)">Field Marshal</a> <a href="/wiki/Sir_William_Robertson,_1st_Baronet" title="Sir William Robertson, 1st Baronet">Sir William Robertson</a>, to add his name to the list.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After graduating from the Staff College, he was appointed <a href="/wiki/Brigade_major" title="Brigade major">brigade major</a> in the <a href="/wiki/17th_Infantry_Brigade_(United_Kingdom)" title="17th Infantry Brigade (United Kingdom)">17th Infantry Brigade</a> in January 1921.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> The brigade was stationed in <a href="/wiki/County_Cork" title="County Cork">County Cork</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>, carrying out counter-insurgency operations during the final stages of the <a href="/wiki/Irish_War_of_Independence" title="Irish War of Independence">Irish War of Independence</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-heath214_26-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heath214-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Montgomery came to the conclusion that the conflict could not be won without harsh measures, and that self-government for Ireland was the only feasible solution; in 1923, after the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Free_State" title="Irish Free State">Irish Free State</a> and during the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Civil_War" title="Irish Civil War">Irish Civil War</a>, Montgomery wrote to <a href="/wiki/Colonel_(British_Army)" class="mw-redirect" title="Colonel (British Army)">Colonel</a> <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Percival" title="Arthur Percival">Arthur Ernest Percival</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Essex_Regiment" title="Essex Regiment">Essex Regiment</a>:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886047036"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Personally, my whole attention was given to defeating the rebels but it never bothered me a bit how many houses were burnt. I think I regarded all civilians as <a href="/wiki/Sinn_F%C3%A9in" title="Sinn Féin">'Shinners'</a> and I never had any dealings with any of them. My own view is that to win a war of this sort, you must be ruthless. <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Cromwell" title="Oliver Cromwell">Oliver Cromwell</a>, or the Germans, would have settled it in a very short time. Nowadays public opinion precludes such methods, the nation would never allow it, and the politicians would lose their jobs if they sanctioned it. That being so, I consider that <a href="/wiki/David_Lloyd_George" title="David Lloyd George">Lloyd George</a> was right in what he did, if we had gone on we could probably have squashed the rebellion as a temporary measure, but it would have broken out again like an ulcer the moment we removed the troops. I think the rebels would probably [have] refused battles, and hidden their arms etc. until we had gone.<sup id="cite_ref-sheehan_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sheehan-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<p>In May 1923, Montgomery was posted to the <a href="/wiki/49th_(West_Riding)_Infantry_Division" title="49th (West Riding) Infantry Division">49th (West Riding) Infantry Division</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Army_Reserve_(United_Kingdom)" title="Army Reserve (United Kingdom)">Territorial Army</a> (TA) formation.<sup id="cite_ref-heath214_26-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heath214-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> He returned to the 1st Battalion, Royal Warwickshire Regiment in 1925 as a <a href="/wiki/Company_commander" title="Company commander">company commander</a><sup id="cite_ref-heath214_26-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heath214-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> and was promoted to major in July 1925.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> From January 1926 to January 1929 he served as Deputy Assistant Adjutant General at the <a href="/wiki/Staff_College,_Camberley" title="Staff College, Camberley">Staff College, Camberley</a>, in the temporary rank of <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_colonel_(United_Kingdom)" title="Lieutenant colonel (United Kingdom)">lieutenant colonel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marriage_and_family">Marriage and family</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bernard_Montgomery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Marriage and family">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1925, in his first known courtship of a woman, Montgomery, then in his late thirties, proposed to a 17-year-old girl, Miss Betty Anderson. His approach included drawing diagrams in the sand of how he would deploy his tanks and infantry in a future war, a contingency which seemed very remote at that time. She respected his ambition and single-mindedness, but declined his proposal of marriage.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1927, he met and married Elizabeth (Betty) Carver, <a href="/wiki/Given_name#Name_at_birth" title="Given name"><span title="Name at birth">n&#233;e</span></a> Hobart, widow of <a href="/wiki/Oswald_Carver" title="Oswald Carver">Oswald Carver</a>, Olympic rowing medallist who had been killed in the First World War.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Betty Carver was the sister of the future Second World War commander, <a href="/wiki/Major-general_(United_Kingdom)" title="Major-general (United Kingdom)">Major General</a> <a href="/wiki/Percy_Hobart" title="Percy Hobart">Sir Percy Hobart</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-heath214_26-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heath214-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Betty Carver had two sons in their early teens, John and Dick, from her first marriage. Dick Carver later wrote that it had been "a very brave thing" for Montgomery to take on a widow with two children.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Montgomery's son, <a href="/wiki/David_Montgomery,_2nd_Viscount_Montgomery_of_Alamein" title="David Montgomery, 2nd Viscount Montgomery of Alamein">David</a>, was born in August 1928.<sup id="cite_ref-heath214_26-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heath214-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>While on holiday in <a href="/wiki/Burnham-on-Sea" title="Burnham-on-Sea">Burnham-on-Sea</a> in 1937, Betty suffered an insect bite which became infected, and she died in her husband's arms from <a href="/wiki/Septicaemia" class="mw-redirect" title="Septicaemia">septicaemia</a> following <a href="/wiki/Amputation" title="Amputation">amputation</a> of her leg.<sup id="cite_ref-heath214_26-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heath214-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The loss devastated Montgomery, who was then serving as a brigadier, but he insisted on throwing himself back into his work immediately after the funeral.<sup id="cite_ref-biermansmith_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biermansmith-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Montgomery's marriage had been extremely happy. Much of his correspondence with his wife was destroyed when his quarters at Portsmouth were bombed during the Second World War.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> After Montgomery's death, John Carver wrote that his mother had arguably done the country a favour by keeping his personal oddities – his extreme single-mindedness, and his intolerance of and suspicion of the motives of others – within reasonable bounds long enough for him to have a chance of attaining high command.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Both of Montgomery's stepsons became army officers in the 1930s (both were serving in India at the time of their mother's death), and both served in the Second World War, each eventually attaining the rank of Colonel.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> While serving as a GSO2<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> with Eighth Army, Dick Carver was sent forward during the pursuit after El Alamein to help identify a new site for Eighth Army HQ. He was taken prisoner at Mersa Matruh on 7 November 1942.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Montgomery wrote to his contacts in England asking that inquiries be made via the <a href="/wiki/Red_Cross" class="mw-redirect" title="Red Cross">Red Cross</a> as to where his stepson was being held, and that parcels be sent to him.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Like many British POWs, the most famous being General <a href="/wiki/Richard_O%27Connor" title="Richard O&#39;Connor">Richard O'Connor</a>, Dick Carver escaped in September 1943 during the brief hiatus between Italy's departure from the war and the German seizure of the country. He eventually reached British lines on 5 December 1943, to the delight of his stepfather, who sent him home to Britain to recuperate.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1930s">1930s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bernard_Montgomery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1930s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In January 1929 Montgomery was promoted to <a href="/wiki/Brevet_(military)" title="Brevet (military)">brevet</a> <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_colonel" title="Lieutenant colonel">lieutenant colonel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> That month he returned to the 1st Battalion, Royal Warwickshire Regiment again, as Commander of Headquarters Company; he went to the <a href="/wiki/War_Office" title="War Office">War Office</a> to help write the Infantry Training Manual in mid-1929.<sup id="cite_ref-heath214_26-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heath214-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> In 1931 Montgomery was promoted to substantive lieutenant colonel<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> and became the <a href="/wiki/Commanding_officer" title="Commanding officer">Commanding Officer</a> (CO) of the 1st Battalion, Royal Warwickshire Regiment and saw service in <a href="/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine" title="Mandatory Palestine">Palestine</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">British India</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-heath214_26-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heath214-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> He was promoted to <a href="/wiki/Colonel_(United_Kingdom)" title="Colonel (United Kingdom)">colonel</a> in June 1934 (seniority from January 1932).<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> He attended and was then recommended to become an instructor at the <a href="/wiki/British_Indian_Army" title="British Indian Army">Indian Army</a> <a href="/wiki/Command_and_Staff_College" title="Command and Staff College">Staff College</a> (now the <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_Army" title="Pakistan Army">Pakistan Army</a> Staff College) in <a href="/wiki/Quetta" title="Quetta">Quetta</a>, British India.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On completion of his tour of duty in India, Montgomery returned to Britain in June 1937<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> where he took command of the <a href="/wiki/9th_Infantry_Brigade_(United_Kingdom)" title="9th Infantry Brigade (United Kingdom)">9th Infantry Brigade</a> with the temporary rank of <a href="/wiki/Brigadier_(United_Kingdom)" title="Brigadier (United Kingdom)">brigadier</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> His wife died that year.<sup id="cite_ref-heath214_26-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heath214-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1938, he organised an <a href="/wiki/Amphibious_warfare" title="Amphibious warfare">amphibious</a> <a href="/wiki/Combined_operations" title="Combined operations">combined operations</a> landing exercise that impressed the new C-in-C of <a href="/wiki/Southern_Command_(United_Kingdom)" title="Southern Command (United Kingdom)">Southern Command</a>, General <a href="/wiki/Archibald_Wavell,_1st_Earl_Wavell" title="Archibald Wavell, 1st Earl Wavell">Sir Archibald Percival Wavell</a>. He was promoted to major general on 14 October 1938<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> and took command of the <a href="/wiki/8th_Infantry_Division_(United_Kingdom)" title="8th Infantry Division (United Kingdom)">8th Infantry Division</a><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> in Palestine.<sup id="cite_ref-heath214_26-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heath214-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> There he quashed an Arab revolt before returning in July 1939 to Britain, suffering a serious illness on the way, to command the <a href="/wiki/3rd_Division_(United_Kingdom)" title="3rd Division (United Kingdom)">3rd (Iron) Infantry Division</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-heath214_26-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heath214-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> On hearing of the rebel defeat in April 1939, Montgomery said, "I shall be sorry to leave Palestine in many ways, as I have enjoyed the war out here".<sup id="cite_ref-biermansmith_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biermansmith-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_World_War">Second World War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bernard_Montgomery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Second World War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="British_Expeditionary_Force">British Expeditionary Force</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bernard_Montgomery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: British Expeditionary Force">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Retreat_to_Dunkirk_and_evacuation">Retreat to Dunkirk and evacuation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bernard_Montgomery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Retreat to Dunkirk and evacuation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a></div>
<p>Britain declared war on Germany on 3 September 1939. The 3rd Division was deployed to Belgium as part of the <a href="/wiki/British_Expeditionary_Force_(World_War_II)" title="British Expeditionary Force (World War II)">British Expeditionary Force</a> (BEF). During this time, Montgomery faced serious trouble from his military superiors and the clergy for his frank attitude regarding the sexual health of his soldiers, but was defended from dismissal by his superior <a href="/wiki/Alan_Brooke,_1st_Viscount_Alanbrooke" title="Alan Brooke, 1st Viscount Alanbrooke">Alan Brooke</a>, commander of <a href="/wiki/British_II_Corps" class="mw-redirect" title="British II Corps">II Corps</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Montgomery's training paid off when the Germans began their invasion of the <a href="/wiki/Low_Countries" title="Low Countries">Low Countries</a> on 10 May 1940 and the 3rd Division advanced to the River <a href="/wiki/Dijle" class="mw-redirect" title="Dijle">Dijle</a> and then withdrew to <a href="/wiki/Dunkirk,_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Dunkirk, France">Dunkirk</a> with great professionalism, entering the Dunkirk perimeter in a famous night-time march that placed his forces on the left flank, which had been left exposed by the Belgian surrender.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> The 3rd Division returned to Britain intact with minimal casualties. During <a href="/wiki/Operation_Dynamo" class="mw-redirect" title="Operation Dynamo">Operation Dynamo</a> — the evacuation of 330,000 BEF and French troops to Britain — Montgomery assumed command of the <a href="/wiki/II_Corps_(United_Kingdom)" title="II Corps (United Kingdom)">II Corps</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-heath216_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heath216-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On his return Montgomery antagonised the <a href="/wiki/War_Office" title="War Office">War Office</a> with trenchant criticisms of the command of the BEF<sup id="cite_ref-biermansmith_19-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biermansmith-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> and was briefly relegated back to divisional command of 3rd Division.  3rd Division was at that time the only fully equipped division in Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-memoirs64_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-memoirs64-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> He was made a <a href="/wiki/Companion_of_the_Order_of_the_Bath" class="mw-redirect" title="Companion of the Order of the Bath">Companion of the Order of the Bath</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cb_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cb-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_British_Army_in_the_United_Kingdom_1939-45_H8492.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/The_British_Army_in_the_United_Kingdom_1939-45_H8492.jpg/220px-The_British_Army_in_the_United_Kingdom_1939-45_H8492.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="216" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/The_British_Army_in_the_United_Kingdom_1939-45_H8492.jpg/330px-The_British_Army_in_the_United_Kingdom_1939-45_H8492.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/The_British_Army_in_the_United_Kingdom_1939-45_H8492.jpg/440px-The_British_Army_in_the_United_Kingdom_1939-45_H8492.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="784" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_British_Army_in_the_United_Kingdom_1939-45_H8492.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lieutenant General Bernard Montgomery, GOC V Corps, with war correspondents during a large-scale exercise in Southern Command, March 1941.</div></div></div>
<p>Montgomery was ordered to make ready his 3rd Division to invade the neutral <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portuguese</a> <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-memoirs64_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-memoirs64-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Models of the islands were prepared and detailed plans worked out for the invasion.<sup id="cite_ref-memoirs64_57-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-memoirs64-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> The invasion plans did not go ahead and plans switched to invading <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">Cape Verde</a> island also belonging to neutral Portugal.<sup id="cite_ref-memoirs65_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-memoirs65-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> These invasion plans also did not go ahead. Montgomery was then ordered to prepare plans for the invasion of neutral Ireland and to seize <a href="/wiki/Cork_(city)" title="Cork (city)">Cork</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cobh" title="Cobh">Cobh</a> and Cork harbour.<sup id="cite_ref-memoirs65_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-memoirs65-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> These invasion plans, like those of the Portuguese islands, also did not go ahead and in July 1940, Montgomery was appointed acting lieutenant-general,<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> and placed in command of <a href="/wiki/V_Corps_(United_Kingdom)" title="V Corps (United Kingdom)">V Corps</a>, responsible for the defence of <a href="/wiki/Hampshire" title="Hampshire">Hampshire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dorset" title="Dorset">Dorset</a>, and started a long-running feud with the new <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" title="Commander-in-chief">Commander-in-Chief</a> (C-in-C) of Southern Command, Lieutenant General <a href="/wiki/Claude_Auchinleck" title="Claude Auchinleck">Claude Auchinleck</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-biermansmith_19-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biermansmith-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_British_Army_in_the_United_Kingdom_1939-45_H14377.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/The_British_Army_in_the_United_Kingdom_1939-45_H14377.jpg/220px-The_British_Army_in_the_United_Kingdom_1939-45_H14377.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/The_British_Army_in_the_United_Kingdom_1939-45_H14377.jpg/330px-The_British_Army_in_the_United_Kingdom_1939-45_H14377.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/The_British_Army_in_the_United_Kingdom_1939-45_H14377.jpg/440px-The_British_Army_in_the_United_Kingdom_1939-45_H14377.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="601" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_British_Army_in_the_United_Kingdom_1939-45_H14377.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Senior officers discuss operations during Exercise 'Bumper', 2 October 1941. On the left the Chief Umpire, Lieutenant-General Bernard Montgomery, talks to the C-in-C Home Forces, General Sir Alan Brooke.</div></div></div>
<p>In April 1941, he became commander of <a href="/wiki/XII_Corps_(United_Kingdom)" title="XII Corps (United Kingdom)">XII Corps</a> responsible for the defence of <a href="/wiki/Kent" title="Kent">Kent</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-heath216_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heath216-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> During this period he instituted a regime of continuous training and insisted on high levels of physical fitness for both officers and other ranks. He was ruthless in sacking officers he considered would be unfit for command in action.<sup id="cite_ref-Mead303_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mead303-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Promoted to temporary lieutenant-general in July,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> in December Montgomery was given command of <a href="/wiki/Aldershot_Command" title="Aldershot Command">South-Eastern Command</a><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> overseeing the defence of Kent, <a href="/wiki/Sussex" title="Sussex">Sussex</a> and <a href="/wiki/Surrey" title="Surrey">Surrey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Mead303_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mead303-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He renamed his command the South-Eastern Army to promote offensive spirit. During this time he further developed and rehearsed his ideas and trained his soldiers, culminating in <a href="/wiki/Exercise_Tiger_(1942)" title="Exercise Tiger (1942)">Exercise Tiger</a> in May 1942, a combined forces <a href="/wiki/Military_exercise" title="Military exercise">exercise</a> involving 100,000 troops.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North_Africa_and_Italy">North Africa and Italy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bernard_Montgomery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: North Africa and Italy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id="Montgomery.27s_early_command"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Montgomery's_early_command">Montgomery's early command</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bernard_Montgomery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Montgomery&#039;s early command">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/North_African_Campaign" class="mw-redirect" title="North African Campaign">North African Campaign</a>, <a href="/wiki/Western_Desert_Campaign" class="mw-redirect" title="Western Desert Campaign">Western Desert Campaign</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tunisia_Campaign" class="mw-redirect" title="Tunisia Campaign">Tunisia Campaign</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Italian_Campaign_(World_War_II)" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian Campaign (World War II)">Italian Campaign (World War II)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bernard_Law_Montgomery_1942.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Bernard_Law_Montgomery_1942.jpg/220px-Bernard_Law_Montgomery_1942.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="171" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Bernard_Law_Montgomery_1942.jpg/330px-Bernard_Law_Montgomery_1942.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Bernard_Law_Montgomery_1942.jpg/440px-Bernard_Law_Montgomery_1942.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2853" data-file-height="2213" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bernard_Law_Montgomery_1942.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Montgomery in a <a href="/wiki/M3_Lee" title="M3 Lee">Grant</a> tank in North Africa, November 1942.</div></div></div>
<p>In 1942, a new field commander was required in the Middle East, where Auchinleck was fulfilling both the role of <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" title="Commander-in-chief">Commander-in-Chief</a> (C-in-C) of <a href="/wiki/Middle_East_Command" title="Middle East Command">Middle East Command</a> and commander <a href="/wiki/Eighth_Army_(United_Kingdom)" title="Eighth Army (United Kingdom)">Eighth Army</a>. He had stabilised the Allied position at the <a href="/wiki/First_Battle_of_El_Alamein" title="First Battle of El Alamein">First Battle of El Alamein</a>, but after a visit in August 1942, the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">Prime Minister</a>, <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a>, replaced him as C-in-C with General <a href="/wiki/Harold_Alexander,_1st_Earl_Alexander_of_Tunis" title="Harold Alexander, 1st Earl Alexander of Tunis">Sir Harold Alexander</a> and <a href="/wiki/William_Gott" title="William Gott">William Gott</a> as commander of the Eighth Army in the <a href="/wiki/Western_Desert_Campaign" class="mw-redirect" title="Western Desert Campaign">Western Desert</a>. However, after Gott was killed flying back to <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a> Churchill was persuaded by Brooke, who by this time was <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_the_General_Staff_(United_Kingdom)" title="Chief of the General Staff (United Kingdom)">Chief of the Imperial General Staff</a> (CIGS), to appoint Montgomery, who had only just been nominated to replace Alexander as commander of the <a href="/wiki/First_Army_(United_Kingdom)" title="First Army (United Kingdom)">British First Army</a> for <a href="/wiki/Operation_Torch" title="Operation Torch">Operation Torch</a>, the invasion of <a href="/wiki/French_North_Africa" title="French North Africa">French North Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A story, probably apocryphal but popular at the time, is that the appointment caused Montgomery to remark that "After having an easy war, things have now got much more difficult." A colleague is supposed to have told him to cheer up – at which point Montgomery said "I'm not talking about me, I'm talking about <a href="/wiki/Erwin_Rommel" title="Erwin Rommel">Rommel</a>!"<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Montgomery's assumption of command transformed the fighting spirit and abilities of the Eighth Army.<sup id="cite_ref-Playfair370_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Playfair370-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Taking command on 13 August 1942, he immediately became a whirlwind of activity. He ordered the creation of the <a href="/wiki/X_Corps_(United_Kingdom)" title="X Corps (United Kingdom)">X Corps</a>, which contained all armoured divisions, to fight alongside his <a href="/wiki/XXX_Corps_(United_Kingdom)" title="XXX Corps (United Kingdom)">XXX Corps</a>, which was all infantry divisions. This arrangement differed from the German Panzer Corps: one of Rommel's Panzer Corps combined infantry, armour and artillery units under one corps commander. The only common commander for Montgomery's all-infantry and all-armour corps was the Eighth Army Commander himself. <a href="/wiki/Correlli_Barnett" title="Correlli Barnett">Correlli Barnett</a> commented that Montgomery's solution "...&#160;was in every way opposite to Auchinleck's and in every way wrong, for it carried the existing dangerous separatism still further."<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Montgomery reinforced the 30 miles (48&#160;km) long front line at El Alamein, something that would take two months to accomplish. He asked Alexander to send him two new British divisions (<a href="/wiki/51st_(Highland)_Division" title="51st (Highland) Division">51st Highland</a> and <a href="/wiki/44th_(Home_Counties)_Division" title="44th (Home Counties) Division">44th Home Counties</a>) that were then arriving in Egypt and were scheduled to be deployed in defence of the Nile Delta. He moved his field HQ to Burg al Arab, close to the Air Force command post in order better to coordinate combined operations.<sup id="cite_ref-Playfair370_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Playfair370-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Montgomery was determined that the Army, Navy and Air Forces should fight their battles in a unified, focused manner according to a detailed plan. He ordered immediate reinforcement of the vital heights of Alam Halfa, just behind his own lines, expecting the German commander, <a href="/wiki/Erwin_Rommel" title="Erwin Rommel">Erwin Rommel</a>, to attack with the heights as his objective, something that Rommel soon did. Montgomery ordered all contingency plans for retreat to be destroyed. "I have cancelled the plan for withdrawal. If we are attacked, then there will be no retreat. If we cannot stay here alive, then we will stay here dead",<sup id="cite_ref-Moorehead118-127_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moorehead118-127-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> he told his officers at the first meeting he held with them in the desert, though, in fact, Auchinleck had no plans to withdraw from the strong defensive position he had chosen and established at El Alamein.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_British_Army_in_North_Africa_1942_E15787.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/The_British_Army_in_North_Africa_1942_E15787.jpg/220px-The_British_Army_in_North_Africa_1942_E15787.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/The_British_Army_in_North_Africa_1942_E15787.jpg/330px-The_British_Army_in_North_Africa_1942_E15787.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/The_British_Army_in_North_Africa_1942_E15787.jpg/440px-The_British_Army_in_North_Africa_1942_E15787.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="584" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_British_Army_in_North_Africa_1942_E15787.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lieutenant-General Bernard Montgomery, the new commander of the British Eighth Army, and Lieutenant-General <a href="/wiki/Brian_Horrocks" title="Brian Horrocks">Brian Horrocks</a>, the new GOC XIII Corps, discussing troop dispositions at 22nd Armoured Brigade HQ, 20 August 1942. The brigade commander, Brigadier <a href="/wiki/George_Philip_Bradley_Roberts" class="mw-redirect" title="George Philip Bradley Roberts">George Roberts</a> is on the right (in beret).</div></div></div>
<p>Montgomery made a great effort to appear before troops as often as possible, frequently visiting various units and making himself known to the men, often arranging for cigarettes to be distributed. Although he still wore a standard British officer's cap on arrival in the desert, he briefly wore an Australian broad-brimmed hat before switching to wearing the black beret (with the badge of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Tank_Regiment" title="Royal Tank Regiment">Royal Tank Regiment</a> next to the British General Officer's badge) for which he became notable. The black beret was offered to him by Jim Fraser while the latter was driving him on an inspection tour.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Both Brooke and Alexander were astonished by the transformation in atmosphere when they visited on 19 August, less than a week after Montgomery had taken command.<sup id="cite_ref-Moorehead118-127_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moorehead118-127-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="First_battles_with_Rommel">First battles with Rommel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bernard_Montgomery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: First battles with Rommel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Animals_in_War_1939-1945_B6541.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Animals_in_War_1939-1945_B6541.jpg/220px-Animals_in_War_1939-1945_B6541.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="221" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Animals_in_War_1939-1945_B6541.jpg/330px-Animals_in_War_1939-1945_B6541.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Animals_in_War_1939-1945_B6541.jpg/440px-Animals_in_War_1939-1945_B6541.jpg 2x" data-file-width="796" data-file-height="800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Animals_in_War_1939-1945_B6541.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>General Montgomery with his pets, the puppies "Hitler" (left) and "Rommel", and a cage of canaries which also travelled with him (France; date unknown).</div></div></div>
<p>Rommel attempted to turn the left flank of the Eighth Army at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Alam_el_Halfa" title="Battle of Alam el Halfa">Battle of Alam el Halfa</a> from 31 August 1942. The German/Italian armoured Corps infantry attack was stopped in very heavy fighting. Rommel's forces had to withdraw urgently lest their retreat through the British minefields be cut off.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Montgomery was criticised for not counter-attacking the retreating forces immediately, but he felt strongly that his methodical build-up of British forces was not yet ready. A hasty counter-attack risked ruining his strategy for an offensive on his own terms in late October, planning for which had begun soon after he took command.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> He was confirmed in the permanent rank of lieutenant-general in mid October.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The conquest of Libya was essential for airfields to support <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a> and to threaten the rear of Axis forces opposing <a href="/wiki/Operation_Torch" title="Operation Torch">Operation Torch</a>. Montgomery prepared meticulously for the new offensive after convincing Churchill that the time was not being wasted. (Churchill sent a telegram to Alexander on 23 September 1942 which began, "We are in your hands and of course a victorious battle makes amends for much delay."<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>) He was determined not to fight until he thought there had been sufficient preparation for a decisive victory, and put into action his beliefs with the gathering of resources, detailed planning, the training of troops—especially in clearing minefields and fighting at night<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>—and in the use of 252<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> of the latest American-built <a href="/wiki/Sherman_tank" class="mw-redirect" title="Sherman tank">Sherman tanks</a>, 90 <a href="/wiki/M7_Priest" title="M7 Priest">M7 Priest</a> self-propelled howitzers, and making a personal visit to every unit involved in the offensive. By the time the offensive was ready in late October, Eighth Army had 231,000 men on its ration strength.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="El_Alamein">El Alamein</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bernard_Montgomery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: El Alamein">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:El_Alamein_1942_-_British_infantry.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/El_Alamein_1942_-_British_infantry.jpg/220px-El_Alamein_1942_-_British_infantry.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="219" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/El_Alamein_1942_-_British_infantry.jpg/330px-El_Alamein_1942_-_British_infantry.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/El_Alamein_1942_-_British_infantry.jpg/440px-El_Alamein_1942_-_British_infantry.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1784" data-file-height="1772" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:El_Alamein_1942_-_British_infantry.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Men of the <a href="/wiki/9th_Division_(Australia)" title="9th Division (Australia)">9th Australian Division</a> in a posed photograph during the <a href="/wiki/Second_Battle_of_El_Alamein" title="Second Battle of El Alamein">Second Battle of El Alamein</a> (photographer: Len Chetwyn)</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Second_Battle_of_El_Alamein" title="Second Battle of El Alamein">Second Battle of El Alamein</a> began on 23 October 1942, and ended 12 days later with one of the first large-scale, decisive Allied land victories of the war. Montgomery correctly predicted both the length of the battle and the number of casualties (13,500).<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Soon after Allied armoured units and infantry broke through the German and Italian lines and were pursuing the enemy forces at speed along the coast road, a violent rainstorm burst over the region, bogging down the tanks and support trucks in the desert mud. Montgomery, standing before his officers at headquarters and close to tears, announced that he was going to call off the pursuit.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Historian" title="Historian">Historian</a> <a href="/wiki/Corelli_Barnett" class="mw-redirect" title="Corelli Barnett">Corelli Barnett</a> has pointed out that the rain also fell on the Germans, and that the weather is therefore an inadequate explanation for the failure to exploit the breakthrough, but nevertheless the Battle of El Alamein had been a great success. Over 30,000 <a href="/wiki/Prisoner_of_war" title="Prisoner of war">prisoners of war</a> were taken,<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> including the German second-in-command, <a href="/wiki/Ritter_von_Thoma" class="mw-redirect" title="Ritter von Thoma">General von Thoma</a>, as well as eight other general officers.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> Rommel, having been in a hospital in Germany at the start of the battle, was forced to return on 25 October 1942 after <a href="/wiki/Georg_Stumme" title="Georg Stumme">Stumme</a> – his replacement as German commander – died of a heart attack in the early hours of the battle.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tunisia">Tunisia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bernard_Montgomery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Tunisia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Campaign_in_North_Africa_1940-1943-_Personalities_E22271.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/The_Campaign_in_North_Africa_1940-1943-_Personalities_E22271.jpg/220px-The_Campaign_in_North_Africa_1940-1943-_Personalities_E22271.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="229" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/The_Campaign_in_North_Africa_1940-1943-_Personalities_E22271.jpg/330px-The_Campaign_in_North_Africa_1940-1943-_Personalities_E22271.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/The_Campaign_in_North_Africa_1940-1943-_Personalities_E22271.jpg/440px-The_Campaign_in_North_Africa_1940-1943-_Personalities_E22271.jpg 2x" data-file-width="767" data-file-height="799" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Campaign_in_North_Africa_1940-1943-_Personalities_E22271.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> with military leaders during his visit to Tripoli. The group includes: Lieutenant-General <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Leese" title="Oliver Leese">Sir Oliver Leese</a>, General <a href="/wiki/Harold_Alexander,_1st_Earl_Alexander_of_Tunis" title="Harold Alexander, 1st Earl Alexander of Tunis">Sir Harold Alexander</a>, General <a href="/wiki/Alan_Brooke,_1st_Viscount_Alanbrooke" title="Alan Brooke, 1st Viscount Alanbrooke">Sir Alan Brooke</a> and General Sir Bernard Montgomery.</div></div></div>
<p>Montgomery was advanced to <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Bath" title="Order of the Bath">KCB</a> and promoted to full <a href="/wiki/General_(United_Kingdom)" title="General (United Kingdom)">general</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-KCB+Gen_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KCB+Gen-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> He kept the initiative, applying superior strength when it suited him, forcing Rommel out of each successive defensive position. On 6 March 1943, Rommel's attack on the over-extended Eighth Army at <a href="/wiki/Medenine" title="Medenine">Medenine</a> (<a href="/wiki/Operation_Capri" class="mw-redirect" title="Operation Capri">Operation Capri</a>) with the largest concentration of German armour in North Africa was successfully repulsed.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/Mareth_Line" title="Mareth Line">Mareth Line</a>, 20 to 27 March, when Montgomery encountered fiercer frontal opposition than he had anticipated, he switched his major effort into an outflanking inland pincer, backed by low-flying <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">RAF</a> fighter-bomber support.<sup id="cite_ref-odnb_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-odnb-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> For his role in North Africa he was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Legion_of_Merit" title="Legion of Merit">Legion of Merit</a> by the United States government in the rank of Chief Commander.<sup id="cite_ref-LM_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LM-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sicily">Sicily</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bernard_Montgomery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Sicily">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gen._Bernard_Law_Montgomery_and_Lt._Gen._George_S._Patton,_Jr.,.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Gen._Bernard_Law_Montgomery_and_Lt._Gen._George_S._Patton%2C_Jr.%2C.jpg/220px-Gen._Bernard_Law_Montgomery_and_Lt._Gen._George_S._Patton%2C_Jr.%2C.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="221" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Gen._Bernard_Law_Montgomery_and_Lt._Gen._George_S._Patton%2C_Jr.%2C.jpg/330px-Gen._Bernard_Law_Montgomery_and_Lt._Gen._George_S._Patton%2C_Jr.%2C.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Gen._Bernard_Law_Montgomery_and_Lt._Gen._George_S._Patton%2C_Jr.%2C.jpg/440px-Gen._Bernard_Law_Montgomery_and_Lt._Gen._George_S._Patton%2C_Jr.%2C.jpg 2x" data-file-width="795" data-file-height="800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gen._Bernard_Law_Montgomery_and_Lt._Gen._George_S._Patton,_Jr.,.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Montgomery visits Patton in Palermo, Sicily, July 1943.</div></div></div>
<p>The next major Allied attack was the <a href="/wiki/Allied_invasion_of_Sicily" title="Allied invasion of Sicily">Allied invasion of Sicily</a> (Operation Husky). Montgomery considered the initial plans for the Allied invasion, which had been agreed in principle by <a href="/wiki/General_(United_States)" title="General (United States)">General</a> <a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight D. Eisenhower</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Allied_Commander" title="Supreme Allied Commander">Supreme Allied Commander</a> <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Theater_of_Operations" title="Mediterranean Theater of Operations">Mediterranean</a>, and General Alexander, the <a href="/wiki/15th_Army_Group" title="15th Army Group">15th Army Group</a> commander, to be unworkable because of the dispersion of effort. He managed to have the plans recast to concentrate the Allied forces, having <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_general_(United_States)" title="Lieutenant general (United States)">Lieutenant General</a> <a href="/wiki/George_S._Patton" title="George S. Patton">George Patton</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Seventh_United_States_Army" title="Seventh United States Army">US Seventh Army</a> land in the Gulf of Gela (on the Eighth Army's left flank, which landed around <a href="/wiki/Syracuse,_Sicily" title="Syracuse, Sicily">Syracuse</a> in the south-east of Sicily) rather than near <a href="/wiki/Palermo" title="Palermo">Palermo</a> in the west and north of Sicily.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> Inter-Allied tensions grew as the American commanders, Patton and <a href="/wiki/Omar_Bradley" title="Omar Bradley">Omar Bradley</a> (then commanding <a href="/wiki/II_Corps_(United_States)" title="II Corps (United States)">US II Corps</a> under Patton), took umbrage at what they saw as Montgomery's attitudes and boastfulness.<sup id="cite_ref-odnb_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-odnb-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> However, while all three were considered three of the greatest soldiers of their time, due to their competitiveness they were renowned for ‘squabbling like three schoolgirls’ thanks to their ‘bitchiness’, ‘whining to their superiors’ and ‘showing off’.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Italian_campaign">Italian campaign</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bernard_Montgomery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Italian campaign">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Montgomery_E010786478-v8.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Montgomery_E010786478-v8.jpg/170px-Montgomery_E010786478-v8.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="218" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Montgomery_E010786478-v8.jpg/255px-Montgomery_E010786478-v8.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Montgomery_E010786478-v8.jpg/340px-Montgomery_E010786478-v8.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="1283" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Montgomery_E010786478-v8.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wartime photograph of General Sir Bernard Montgomery with his <a href="/wiki/Miles_Messenger" title="Miles Messenger">Miles Messenger</a> aircraft (location and date unknown).</div></div></div>
<p>During late 1943, Montgomery continued to command the Eighth Army during the <a href="/wiki/Allied_invasion_of_Italy" title="Allied invasion of Italy">landings on the mainland of Italy itself</a>, beginning with <a href="/wiki/Operation_Baytown" title="Operation Baytown">Operation Baytown</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-heath217_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heath217-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> In conjunction with the Anglo-American <a href="/wiki/Allied_invasion_of_Italy#Salerno_landings" title="Allied invasion of Italy">landings at Salerno</a> (near <a href="/wiki/Naples" title="Naples">Naples</a>) by <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_general_(United_States)" title="Lieutenant general (United States)">Lieutenant General</a> <a href="/wiki/Mark_W._Clark" title="Mark W. Clark">Mark Clark</a>'s <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_North" title="United States Army North">US Fifth Army</a> and <a href="/wiki/Operation_Slapstick" title="Operation Slapstick">seaborne landings by British paratroops</a> in the heel of Italy (including the key port of Taranto, where they disembarked without resistance directly into the port), Montgomery led the Eighth Army <a href="/wiki/Italian_Campaign_(World_War_II)" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian Campaign (World War II)">up the toe of Italy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-heath217_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heath217-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> Montgomery abhorred the lack of coordination, the dispersion of effort, the strategic muddle and lack of opportunism he saw in the Allied effort in Italy and was glad to leave the "dog's breakfast" on 23 December 1943.<sup id="cite_ref-odnb_86-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-odnb-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Normandy">Normandy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bernard_Montgomery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Normandy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Normandy" title="Invasion of Normandy">Invasion of Normandy</a></div>
