<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Operationvarsity.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Operationvarsity.jpg/290px-Operationvarsity.jpg" decoding="async" width="290" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Operationvarsity.jpg/435px-Operationvarsity.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Operationvarsity.jpg/580px-Operationvarsity.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Operationvarsity.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Montgomery (left), Air Marshal <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Coningham_(RAF_officer)" title="Arthur Coningham (RAF officer)">Sir Arthur Coningham</a> (centre) and the Commander of the <a href="/wiki/Second_Army_(United_Kingdom)" title="Second Army (United Kingdom)">British Second Army</a>, Lieutenant General <a href="/wiki/Miles_Dempsey" title="Miles Dempsey">Sir Miles Dempsey</a>, talking after a conference in which Montgomery gave the order for the Second Army to begin <a href="/wiki/Operation_Plunder" title="Operation Plunder">Operation Plunder</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Montgomery_receives_Order_of_Victory_HD-SN-99-02756.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Montgomery_receives_Order_of_Victory_HD-SN-99-02756.JPG/220px-Montgomery_receives_Order_of_Victory_HD-SN-99-02756.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="184" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Montgomery_receives_Order_of_Victory_HD-SN-99-02756.JPG/330px-Montgomery_receives_Order_of_Victory_HD-SN-99-02756.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Montgomery_receives_Order_of_Victory_HD-SN-99-02756.JPG/440px-Montgomery_receives_Order_of_Victory_HD-SN-99-02756.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2561" data-file-height="2144" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Montgomery_receives_Order_of_Victory_HD-SN-99-02756.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Montgomery was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Victory" title="Order of Victory">Order of Victory</a> on June 5, 1945. <a href="/wiki/Dwight_Eisenhower" class="mw-redirect" title="Dwight Eisenhower">Dwight Eisenhower</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgy_Zhukov" title="Georgy Zhukov">Georgy Zhukov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sir_Arthur_Tedder" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Arthur Tedder">Sir Arthur Tedder</a> were also present.</div></div></div>
<p>Montgomery's 21st Army Group (later) advanced to the Rhine with operations <a href="/wiki/Operation_Veritable" title="Operation Veritable">Veritable</a> and <a href="/wiki/Operation_Grenade" title="Operation Grenade">Grenade</a> in February 1945. A meticulously planned <a href="/wiki/Operation_Plunder" title="Operation Plunder">Rhine crossing</a> occurred on 24 March. While successful, it was two weeks after the Americans had unexpectedly (sans meticulous planning) <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Remagen" title="Battle of Remagen">captured</a> the (railway) <a href="/wiki/Ludendorff_Bridge" title="Ludendorff Bridge">Ludendorff Bridge</a> at Remagen and crossed the river on 7 March.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Montgomery's river crossing was followed by the <a href="/wiki/Ruhr_Pocket" title="Ruhr Pocket">encirclement</a> of German <a href="/wiki/Army_Group_B" title="Army Group B">Army Group B</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Ruhr" title="Ruhr">Ruhr</a>. Initially Montgomery's role was to guard the flank of the American advance. This was altered to forestall any chance of a <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> advance into Denmark, and the 21st Army Group occupied <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rostock" title="Rostock">Rostock</a> and sealed off the Danish peninsula.<sup id="cite_ref-odnb_86-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-odnb-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> On 4 May 1945, on <a href="/wiki/L%C3%BCneburg_Heath" title="Lüneburg Heath">Lüneburg Heath</a>, Montgomery accepted the <a href="/wiki/German_surrender_at_L%C3%BCneburg_Heath" title="German surrender at Lüneburg Heath">surrender of German forces in north-west Germany, Denmark and the Netherlands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-heath218_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heath218-185">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Casualty_conservation_policy">Casualty conservation policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bernard_Montgomery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Casualty conservation policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The British high command were not concerned only with winning the war by defeating Germany, but also with ensuring that they were still considered to be a serious power after the war, able to influence global policy. Suffering heavy losses in Normandy would diminish Britain's Imperial influence on the post-war world, and on post-war Europe in particular.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHart200755_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHart200755-186">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> Many of Montgomery's clashes with Eisenhower were based on his determination to pursue the war "on lines most suitable to Britain".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHart200756_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHart200756-187">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The fewer the number of combat-experienced divisions the British had left at the end of the war, the smaller Britain's influence in Europe was likely to be, compared to the emerging superpowers of the US and the USSR. Montgomery was thus caught in a dilemma – the British Army needed to be seen to be pulling at least half the weight in the liberation of Europe, but without incurring the heavy casualties that such a role would inevitably produce. The 21st Army Group scarcely possessed sufficient forces to achieve such a military prominence, and the remaining divisions had to be expended sparingly.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHart200758_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHart200758-188">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Britain did not possess the resources in 1944 to rebuild shattered divisions and it was imperative for Montgomery to protect the viability of the British army so that Britain could still play an important part in the final victory. It was reported to the War Office that "Montgomery has to be very careful of what he does on his eastern flank because on that flank is the only British Army there is left in this part of the world". The context of British casualties and the shortage of reinforcements, prompted Montgomery to "excessive caution".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHart200770_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHart200770-189">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> Dempsey wrote on 13 June, that Caen could only be taken by a "set piece assault and we did not have the men or the ammunition for that at the time".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHart200776–77_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHart200776–77-190">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Montgomery's solution to the dilemma was to attempt to remain Commander of All Land Forces until the end of the war, so that any victory attained – although achieved primarily by American formations – would accrue in part to him and thus to Britain. He would also be able to ensure that British units were spared some of the high-attrition actions, but would be most prominent when the final blows were struck.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHart200759_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHart200759-191">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> When that strategy failed, he persuaded Eisenhower to occasionally put some American formations under the control of the 21st Army Group, so as to bolster his resources while still maintaining the outward appearance of successful British effort.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHart200760_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHart200760-192">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Montgomery initially remained prepared to push Second (British) Army hard to capture the vital strategic town of Caen, and consequently incur heavy losses. In the original Overlord plan, Montgomery was determined to push past Caen to Falaise as quickly as possible. However, after the heavy casualties incurred in capturing Caen, he changed his mind.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHart200763_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHart200763-193">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Lack_of_tact">Lack of tact</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bernard_Montgomery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Lack of tact">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Montgomery was notorious for his lack of tact and <a href="/wiki/Diplomacy" title="Diplomacy">diplomacy</a>. Even his "patron", the Chief of the Imperial General Staff <a href="/wiki/Alan_Brooke,_1st_Viscount_Alanbrooke" title="Alan Brooke, 1st Viscount Alanbrooke">Lord Alanbrooke</a>, frequently mentions it in his war diaries: "he is liable to commit untold errors in lack of tact" and  "I had to haul him over the coals for his usual lack of tact and egotistical outlook which prevented him from appreciating other people's feelings".<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>One incident that illustrated this occurred during the North African campaign when Montgomery bet <a href="/wiki/Walter_Bedell_Smith" title="Walter Bedell Smith">Walter Bedell Smith</a> that he could capture <a href="/wiki/Sfax" title="Sfax">Sfax</a> by the middle of April 1943. Smith jokingly replied that if Montgomery could do it he would give him a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_B-17_Flying_Fortress" title="Boeing B-17 Flying Fortress">Flying Fortress</a> complete with crew. Smith promptly forgot all about it, but Montgomery did not, and when Sfax was taken on 10 April he sent a message to Smith "claiming his winnings". Smith tried to laugh it off, but Montgomery was having none of it and insisted on his aircraft. It got as high as <a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Eisenhower</a> who, with his renowned skill in diplomacy, ensured Montgomery did get his Flying Fortress, though at a great cost in ill feeling.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> Even Brooke thought it crass stupidity.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 1945, whilst Brooke, <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Cunningham,_1st_Viscount_Cunningham_of_Hyndhope" title="Andrew Cunningham, 1st Viscount Cunningham of Hyndhope">Sir Andrew Cunningham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charles_Portal,_1st_Viscount_Portal_of_Hungerford" title="Charles Portal, 1st Viscount Portal of Hungerford">Sir Charles Portal</a> were discussing their possible successors as "Chiefs of Staff", they concluded that Montgomery would be very efficient as CIGS from the Army's point of view but that he was also very unpopular with a large proportion of the Army. Despite this, Cunningham and Portal were strongly in favour of Montgomery succeeding Brooke after his retirement.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> Prime Minister Winston Churchill, by all accounts a faithful friend, is quoted as saying of Montgomery, "In defeat, unbeatable; in victory, unbearable."<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_life">Later life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bernard_Montgomery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Later life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bernard_Montgomery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Allies_at_the_Brandenburg_Gate,_1945.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Allies_at_the_Brandenburg_Gate%2C_1945.jpg/220px-Allies_at_the_Brandenburg_Gate%2C_1945.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Allies_at_the_Brandenburg_Gate%2C_1945.jpg/330px-Allies_at_the_Brandenburg_Gate%2C_1945.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Allies_at_the_Brandenburg_Gate%2C_1945.jpg/440px-Allies_at_the_Brandenburg_Gate%2C_1945.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2480" data-file-height="1690" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Allies_at_the_Brandenburg_Gate,_1945.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Montgomery and <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> Marshals <a href="/wiki/Georgy_Zhukov" title="Georgy Zhukov">Zhukov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Konstantin_Rokossovsky" title="Konstantin Rokossovsky">Rokossovsky</a> with General <a href="/wiki/Vasily_Sokolovsky" title="Vasily Sokolovsky">Sokolovsky</a> leave the <a href="/wiki/Brandenburg_Gate" title="Brandenburg Gate">Brandenburg Gate</a> on 12 July 1945 after being decorated by Montgomery.</div></div></div>
<p>After the war Montgomery became the <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" title="Commander-in-chief">Commander-in-Chief</a> (C-in-C) of the <a href="/wiki/British_Army_of_the_Rhine" title="British Army of the Rhine">British Army of the Rhine</a> (BAOR), the name given to the British Occupation Forces, and was the British member of the Allied Control Council.<sup id="cite_ref-Mead309_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mead309-199">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> Montgomery was also President of <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_F.C." title="Portsmouth F.C.">Portsmouth Football Club</a> between 1944 and 1961.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> He was created 1st <a href="/wiki/Viscount_Montgomery_of_Alamein" title="Viscount Montgomery of Alamein">Viscount Montgomery of Alamein</a> in <a href="/wiki/1946_New_Year_Honours" title="1946 New Year Honours">1946</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-viscount_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-viscount-201">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> He was <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_the_General_Staff_(United_Kingdom)" title="Chief of the General Staff (United Kingdom)">Chief of the Imperial General Staff</a> (CIGS) from 1946 to 1948, succeeding Alan Brooke. As CIGS, Montgomery toured Africa in 1947 and in a secret 1948 report to <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Clement_Attlee" title="Clement Attlee">Clement Attlee</a>'s government proposed a "master plan" to exploit the raw materials of Africa, thereby counteracting the loss of British influence in Asia. Montgomery held racist views towards Africans, describing them as "complete savages" incapable of developing their own countries.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> He was barely on speaking terms with his fellow chiefs, sending his VCIGS to attend their meetings<sup id="cite_ref-Mead309_199-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mead309-199">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> and he clashed particularly with <a href="/wiki/Sir_Arthur_Tedder" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Arthur Tedder">Sir Arthur Tedder</a>, who was by now <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_the_Air_Staff_(United_Kingdom)" title="Chief of the Air Staff (United Kingdom)">Chief of the Air Staff</a> (CAS). When Montgomery's term of office expired, Prime Minister Attlee appointed <a href="/wiki/William_Slim,_1st_Viscount_Slim" title="William Slim, 1st Viscount Slim">Sir William Slim</a> from retirement with the rank of <a href="/wiki/Field_Marshal_(United_Kingdom)" class="mw-redirect" title="Field Marshal (United Kingdom)">field marshal</a> as his successor; when Montgomery protested that he had told his protégé, General <a href="/wiki/John_Crocker" title="John Crocker">Sir John Crocker</a>, former commander of <a href="/wiki/I_Corps_(United_Kingdom)" title="I Corps (United Kingdom)">I Corps</a> in the 1944–45 <a href="/wiki/North-West_Europe_Campaign" class="mw-redirect" title="North-West Europe Campaign">North-West Europe Campaign</a>, that the job was to be his, Attlee is said to have retorted "Untell him".<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Field_Marshal_Lord_Montgomery_(19481576520).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Field_Marshal_Lord_Montgomery_%2819481576520%29.jpg/170px-Field_Marshal_Lord_Montgomery_%2819481576520%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="229" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Field_Marshal_Lord_Montgomery_%2819481576520%29.jpg/255px-Field_Marshal_Lord_Montgomery_%2819481576520%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Field_Marshal_Lord_Montgomery_%2819481576520%29.jpg/340px-Field_Marshal_Lord_Montgomery_%2819481576520%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1897" data-file-height="2555" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Field_Marshal_Lord_Montgomery_(19481576520).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Montgomery in <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> in 1947</div></div></div>
<p>He was then appointed Chairman of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Union_Defence_Organization" class="mw-redirect" title="Western Union Defence Organization">Western Union Defence Organization</a>'s C-in-C committee.<sup id="cite_ref-Mead309_199-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mead309-199">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> Volume 3 of <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Hamilton_(author)" title="Nigel Hamilton (author)">Nigel Hamilton</a>'s <i>Life of Montgomery of Alamein</i> gives an account of the bickering between Montgomery and his land forces chief, French General <a href="/wiki/Jean_de_Lattre_de_Tassigny" title="Jean de Lattre de Tassigny">Jean de Lattre de Tassigny</a>, which created splits through the Union headquarters. He was thus pleased to become Eisenhower's deputy in creating the <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">North Atlantic Treaty Organisation</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Headquarters_Allied_Powers_Europe" title="Supreme Headquarters Allied Powers Europe">European</a> forces in 1951.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> He would continue to serve under Eisenhower's successors, Generals <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Ridgway" title="Matthew Ridgway">Matthew Ridgway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Gruenther" title="Alfred Gruenther">Al Gruenther</a>, until his retirement, aged nearly 71, in 1958.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> His mother Maud, <a href="/wiki/Lady" title="Lady">Lady</a> Montgomery, died at New Park in <a href="/wiki/Moville" title="Moville">Moville</a> in <a href="/wiki/Inishowen" title="Inishowen">Inishowen</a> in 1949; she was buried alongside her husband in the '<a href="/wiki/Kirkyard" class="mw-redirect" title="Kirkyard">kirkyard</a>' behind St. Columb's Church, the small <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Ireland" title="Church of Ireland">Church of Ireland</a> church beside New Park, overlooking <a href="/wiki/Lough_Foyle" title="Lough Foyle">Lough Foyle</a>. Montgomery did not attend the funeral, claiming he was "too busy".<sup id="cite_ref-odnb_86-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-odnb-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He was chairman of the governing body of <a href="/wiki/St._John%27s_School,_Leatherhead" class="mw-redirect" title="St. John&#39;s School, Leatherhead">St. John's School</a> in <a href="/wiki/Leatherhead" title="Leatherhead">Leatherhead</a>, <a href="/wiki/Surrey" title="Surrey">Surrey</a>, from 1951 to 1966, and a generous supporter. Montgomery was an Honorary Member of the <a href="/wiki/Winkle_Club" title="Winkle Club">Winkle Club</a>, a charity in <a href="/wiki/Hastings" title="Hastings">Hastings</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Sussex" title="East Sussex">East Sussex</a>, and introduced <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> to the club in 1955.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Views">Views</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bernard_Montgomery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Views">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Monty,_wavvel,_auk.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Monty%2C_wavvel%2C_auk.jpg/220px-Monty%2C_wavvel%2C_auk.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Monty%2C_wavvel%2C_auk.jpg/330px-Monty%2C_wavvel%2C_auk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Monty%2C_wavvel%2C_auk.jpg/440px-Monty%2C_wavvel%2C_auk.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Monty,_wavvel,_auk.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lord Montgomery as <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_the_Imperial_General_Staff" class="mw-redirect" title="Chief of the Imperial General Staff">CIGS</a> with <a href="/wiki/Archibald_Wavell,_1st_Earl_Wavell" title="Archibald Wavell, 1st Earl Wavell">Lord Wavell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Viceroy_of_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Viceroy of India">Viceroy of India</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Claude_Auchinleck" title="Claude Auchinleck">Auchinleck</a>, Commander in Chief Indian Army. Delhi 1946</div></div></div>
<p>Montgomery's memoirs (1958) criticised many of his wartime comrades in harsh terms, including Eisenhower.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> He was threatened with legal action by Field Marshal Auchinleck for suggesting that Auchinleck had intended to retreat from the Alamein position if attacked again, and had to give a radio broadcast (20 November 1958) expressing his gratitude to Auchinleck for having stabilised the front at the First Battle of Alamein.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 1960 paperback edition of his memoirs contains a publisher's note drawing attention to that broadcast, and stating that in the publisher's view the reader might reasonably assume from Montgomery's text that Auchinleck had been planning to retreat "into the Nile Delta or beyond" and pointing out that it had been Auchinleck's intention to launch an offensive as soon as the Eighth Army was "rested and regrouped".<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> Montgomery was stripped of his honorary citizenship of <a href="/wiki/Montgomery,_Alabama" title="Montgomery, Alabama">Montgomery, Alabama</a>, and was challenged to a duel by an Italian officer.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He twice met <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israeli</a> general <a href="/wiki/Moshe_Dayan" title="Moshe Dayan">Moshe Dayan</a>. After an initial meeting in the early 1950s, Montgomery met Dayan again in the 1960s to discuss the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a>, which Dayan was studying. Montgomery was harshly critical of US strategy in Vietnam, which involved deploying large numbers of combat troops, aggressive bombing attacks, and uprooting entire village populations and forcing them into <a href="/wiki/Strategic_Hamlet_Program" title="Strategic Hamlet Program">strategic hamlets</a>. Montgomery said that the Americans' most important problem was that they had no clear-cut objective, and allowed local commanders to set military policy. At the end of their meeting, Montgomery asked Dayan to tell the Americans, in his name, that they were "insane".<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> In retirement he publicly supported <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">apartheid</a> after a visit to <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> in 1962, and after a visit to China declared himself impressed by the Chinese leadership.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He spoke out against the legalisation of homosexuality in the United Kingdom, arguing that the <a href="/wiki/Sexual_Offences_Act_1967" title="Sexual Offences Act 1967">Sexual Offences Act 1967</a> was a "charter for buggery"<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> and that "this sort of thing may be tolerated by the French, but we're British – thank God".<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During a visit to the Alamein battlefields in May 1967, he bluntly told high-ranking <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_Army" title="Egyptian Army">Egyptian Army</a> officers that they would lose any war with Israel, a warning that was shown to be justified only a few weeks later in the <a href="/wiki/Six-Day_War" title="Six-Day War">Six-Day War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Death">Death</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bernard_Montgomery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Death">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:112px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BernardMontgomery_Aberdare_Blog_crop.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/BernardMontgomery_Aberdare_Blog_crop.jpg/110px-BernardMontgomery_Aberdare_Blog_crop.jpg" decoding="async" width="110" height="304" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/BernardMontgomery_Aberdare_Blog_crop.jpg/165px-BernardMontgomery_Aberdare_Blog_crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/BernardMontgomery_Aberdare_Blog_crop.jpg/220px-BernardMontgomery_Aberdare_Blog_crop.jpg 2x" data-file-width="594" data-file-height="1641" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BernardMontgomery_Aberdare_Blog_crop.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Statue of Montgomery in <a href="/wiki/Whitehall" title="Whitehall">Whitehall</a>, London, by <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Nemon" title="Oscar Nemon">Oscar Nemon</a>, unveiled in 1980</div></div></div>
<p>Montgomery died from unspecified causes in 1976 at his home Isington Mill in <a href="/wiki/Isington" title="Isington">Isington</a>, in the County of <a href="/wiki/Hampshire" title="Hampshire">Hampshire</a>, aged 88. After a funeral at <a href="/wiki/St_George%27s_Chapel,_Windsor" class="mw-redirect" title="St George&#39;s Chapel, Windsor">St George's Chapel, Windsor</a>, his body was buried in Holy Cross churchyard, in <a href="/wiki/Binsted" title="Binsted">Binsted</a>, Hampshire.<sup id="cite_ref-odnb_86-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-odnb-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>His <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Garter" title="Order of the Garter">Garter banner</a>, which had hung in St. George's Chapel in Windsor during his lifetime, is now on display in <a href="/wiki/Collegiate_Church_of_St_Mary,_Warwick" title="Collegiate Church of St Mary, Warwick">St Mary's, Warwick</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bernard_Montgomery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li>Montgomery's portrait by <a href="/wiki/Frank_O._Salisbury" title="Frank O. Salisbury">Frank O. Salisbury</a> (1945) hangs in the <a href="/wiki/National_Portrait_Gallery_(London)" class="mw-redirect" title="National Portrait Gallery (London)">National Portrait Gallery</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>A statue of Montgomery by <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Nemon" title="Oscar Nemon">Oscar Nemon</a> stands outside the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(United_Kingdom)" title="Ministry of Defence (United Kingdom)">Ministry of Defence</a> in <a href="/wiki/Whitehall" title="Whitehall">Whitehall</a>, alongside those of <a href="/wiki/William_Slim" class="mw-redirect" title="William Slim">Field Marshal Lord Slim</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alan_Brooke,_1st_Viscount_Alanbrooke" title="Alan Brooke, 1st Viscount Alanbrooke">Field Marshal Lord Alanbrooke</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Montgomery gave his name to the French <a href="/wiki/Communes_of_France" title="Communes of France">commune</a> <a href="/wiki/Colleville-Montgomery" title="Colleville-Montgomery">Colleville-Montgomery</a> in Normandy.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:M3_Monty.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/M3_Monty.JPG/220px-M3_Monty.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/M3_Monty.JPG/330px-M3_Monty.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/M3_Monty.JPG/440px-M3_Monty.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:M3_Monty.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Montgomery's Grant command tank, on display at the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_War_Museum" title="Imperial War Museum">Imperial War Museum</a> in London</div></div></div>
<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Imperial_War_Museum" title="Imperial War Museum">Imperial War Museum</a> holds a variety of material relating to Montgomery in its collections. These include Montgomery's <a href="/wiki/M3_Lee" title="M3 Lee">Grant</a> command tank (on display in the atrium at the Museum's London branch), his command caravans as used in North West Europe (on display at IWM Duxford), and his papers are held by the Museum's Department of Documents. The Museum maintains a permanent exhibition about Montgomery, entitled <i>Monty: Master of the Battlefield</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/World_Pipe_Band_Championships" title="World Pipe Band Championships">World Champion</a> <a href="/wiki/Field_Marshal_Montgomery_Pipe_Band" title="Field Marshal Montgomery Pipe Band">Field Marshal Montgomery Pipe Band</a> from <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a> is named after him.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Montgomery's <a href="/wiki/List_of_Rolls-Royce_motor_cars" title="List of Rolls-Royce motor cars">Rolls-Royce</a> staff car is on display at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Logistic_Corps_Museum" title="Royal Logistic Corps Museum">Royal Logistic Corps Museum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deepcut" title="Deepcut">Deepcut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Surrey" title="Surrey">Surrey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>The Montgomery cocktail is a <a href="/wiki/Martini_(cocktail)" title="Martini (cocktail)">martini</a> mixed at a ratio of 15 parts gin to 1 part vermouth, and popular with <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Hemingway" title="Ernest Hemingway">Ernest Hemingway</a> at <a href="/wiki/Harry%27s_Bar_(Venice)" title="Harry&#39;s Bar (Venice)">Harry's Bar</a> in Venice.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> The drink was facetiously named for Montgomery's supposed refusal to go into battle unless his numerical advantage was at least fifteen to one, and it appeared in Hemingway's 1950 novel <i><a href="/wiki/Across_the_River_and_into_the_Trees" title="Across the River and into the Trees">Across the River and into the Trees</a></i>. Ironically, following severe internal injuries received in the First World War, Montgomery himself could neither smoke nor drink.<sup id="cite_ref-Lanning_161-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lanning-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honours_and_awards">Honours and awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bernard_Montgomery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Honours and awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_Arms_of_Bernard_Montgomery,_1st_Viscount_Montgomery_of_Alamein,_KG,_GCB,_DSO,_PC,_DL.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Coat_of_Arms_of_Bernard_Montgomery%2C_1st_Viscount_Montgomery_of_Alamein%2C_KG%2C_GCB%2C_DSO%2C_PC%2C_DL.png/220px-Coat_of_Arms_of_Bernard_Montgomery%2C_1st_Viscount_Montgomery_of_Alamein%2C_KG%2C_GCB%2C_DSO%2C_PC%2C_DL.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Coat_of_Arms_of_Bernard_Montgomery%2C_1st_Viscount_Montgomery_of_Alamein%2C_KG%2C_GCB%2C_DSO%2C_PC%2C_DL.png/330px-Coat_of_Arms_of_Bernard_Montgomery%2C_1st_Viscount_Montgomery_of_Alamein%2C_KG%2C_GCB%2C_DSO%2C_PC%2C_DL.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Coat_of_Arms_of_Bernard_Montgomery%2C_1st_Viscount_Montgomery_of_Alamein%2C_KG%2C_GCB%2C_DSO%2C_PC%2C_DL.png/440px-Coat_of_Arms_of_Bernard_Montgomery%2C_1st_Viscount_Montgomery_of_Alamein%2C_KG%2C_GCB%2C_DSO%2C_PC%2C_DL.png 2x" data-file-width="1158" data-file-height="1158" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_Arms_of_Bernard_Montgomery,_1st_Viscount_Montgomery_of_Alamein,_KG,_GCB,_DSO,_PC,_DL.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Garter-encircled coat of arms of Bernard Montgomery, 1st Viscount Montgomery of Alamein, KG, as displayed on his Order of the Garter stall plate in St. George's Chapel, Windsor Castle, viz. Azure two lions passant guardant between three fleur-de-lis two in chief and one in base and two trefoils in fess all or.</div></div></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Viscountcy" class="mw-redirect" title="Viscountcy">Viscountcy</a> as <i><a href="/wiki/Viscount_Montgomery_of_Alamein" title="Viscount Montgomery of Alamein">Montgomery of Alamein</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">UK</a>, January 1946)<sup id="cite_ref-viscount_201-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-viscount-201">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Knight_of_the_Most_Noble_Order_of_the_Garter" class="mw-redirect" title="Knight of the Most Noble Order of the Garter">Knight of the Most Noble Order of the Garter</a> (UK, 1946)<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Knight_Grand_Cross_of_the_Most_Honourable_Order_of_the_Bath" class="mw-redirect" title="Knight Grand Cross of the Most Honourable Order of the Bath">Knight Grand Cross of the Most Honourable Order of the Bath</a> (UK, 1945)<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> KCB – 11 November 1942,<sup id="cite_ref-KCB+Gen_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KCB+Gen-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> CB – 11 July 1940<sup id="cite_ref-cb_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cb-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Companion_of_the_Distinguished_Service_Order" class="mw-redirect" title="Companion of the Distinguished Service Order">Companion of the Distinguished Service Order</a> (UK, 1914)<sup id="cite_ref-DSO_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DSO-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mentioned_in_Despatches" class="mw-redirect" title="Mentioned in Despatches">Mentioned in Despatches</a> (UK, 17 February 1915, 4 January 1917, 11 December 1917, 20 May 1918, 20 December 1918, 5 July 1919, 15 July 1939, 24 June 1943,<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> 13 January 1944<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Distinguished_Service_Medal_(U.S._Army)" title="Distinguished Service Medal (U.S. Army)">Distinguished Service Medal</a> (US, 1947)<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Chief Commander of the <a href="/wiki/Legion_of_Merit" title="Legion of Merit">Legion of Merit</a> (US, 10 August 1943)<sup id="cite_ref-LM_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LM-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Member of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Victory" title="Order of Victory">Order of Victory</a> (<a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">USSR</a>, 21 June 1945)<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>1st class of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Suvorov" title="Order of Suvorov">Order of Suvorov</a> (USSR, 16 January 1947)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Croix_de_guerre_1914%E2%80%931918_(France)" title="Croix de guerre 1914–1918 (France)">Croix de Guerre</a> (France, 1919)<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Knight of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Elephant" title="Order of the Elephant">Order of the Elephant</a> (Denmark, 2 August 1945)<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Grand Commander of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_George_I" title="Order of George I">Order of George I</a> (Greece, 20 June 1944)<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Silver Cross (V Class) of the <a href="/wiki/Virtuti_Militari" title="Virtuti Militari">Virtuti Militari</a> (Poland, 31 October 1944)<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Grand Cross of the <a href="/wiki/Military_Order_of_the_White_Lion" title="Military Order of the White Lion">Military Order of the White Lion</a> (Czechoslovakia, 1947)<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Grand Cordon of the Seal of Solomon (Ethiopia, 1949)<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Grand Officer with Palm of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Leopold_II" title="Order of Leopold II">Order of Leopold II</a> (Belgium, 1947)<sup id="cite_ref-lg37853_236-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lg37853-236">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/War_Cross_(Belgium)" class="mw-redirect" title="War Cross (Belgium)">Croix de Guerre 1940 with Palm</a> (Belgium)<sup id="cite_ref-lg37853_236-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lg37853-236">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Grand Cross of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Netherlands_Lion" title="Order of the Netherlands Lion">Order of the Netherlands Lion</a> (Netherlands, 16 January 1947)<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Grand Cross of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Norwegian_Order_of_St._Olav" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Norwegian Order of St. Olav">Royal Norwegian Order of St. Olav</a> (Norway) (1951)<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Viscount Montgomery's ribbons as they would appear today, not including campaign or other awards.
